<p><b>James Howard</b> "<b>Jim</b>" <b>Thome</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> born August 27, 1970) is a former American <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> player who played 22 seasons in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB), from 1991 to 2012. He played for six different teams, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> during the 1990s and the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> in the early 2000s. A prolific power hitter, Thome hit 612 <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a> during his career—the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_home_run_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career home run leaders">seventh-most all time</a>—along with 2,328 <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hits</a>, 1,699 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a> (RBIs), and a .276 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>. He was a member of five <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> teams and won a <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a> in 1996.</p>
<p>Thome grew up in <a href="/wiki/Peoria,_Illinois" title="Peoria, Illinois">Peoria, Illinois</a>, as part of a large <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue-collar" title="Blue-collar">blue-collar</a> family of athletes, who predominantly played baseball and <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>. After attending <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Central_College" title="Illinois Central College">Illinois Central College</a>, he was drafted by the Indians in <a href="/wiki/1989_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1989 Major League Baseball draft">1989</a> and made his major league debut in 1991. Early in his career, he played <a href="/wiki/Third_baseman" title="Third baseman">third base</a> before eventually becoming a <a href="/wiki/First_baseman" title="First baseman">first baseman</a>. With the Indians, Thome was part of a core of players that led the franchise to two <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> appearances in three years during the mid-1990s. He spent over a decade with Cleveland before leaving via free agency after the 2002 season to join the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>, with whom he spent the following three seasons. Traded to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> before the 2006 season, Thome won the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Comeback_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Comeback Player of the Year Award">Comeback Player of the Year Award</a> that year and reached the <a href="/wiki/500_home_run_club" title="500 home run club">500 home run club</a> during his three-season tenure with the team. By this point in his career, back pain limited Thome to being a <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a>. After stints with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>, he made brief returns to Cleveland and Philadelphia before ending his career with the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Baltimore Orioles</a>. Upon retiring, Thome accepted an executive position with the White Sox.</p>
<p>Throughout his career, Thome's strength was power hitting. In six different seasons, he hit more than 40 home runs, and in 2003, he <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_annual_home_run_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball annual home run leaders">led the National League in home runs</a> with 47. His career <a href="/wiki/On-base_plus_slugging" title="On-base plus slugging">on-base plus slugging</a> (OPS) of .956 is 19th all time. In 2011, he became the eighth MLB player to hit 600 home runs. One of Thome's trademarks was his unique batting stance, in which he held the bat out with his right hand and pointed it at right field before the pitcher threw, something he first saw in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Natural_(film)" title="The Natural (film)">The Natural</a></i>. Thome was known for his consistently positive attitude and "gregarious" personality. An active <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropist</a> during his playing career, he was honored with two <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Miller_Man_of_the_Year_Award" title="Marvin Miller Man of the Year Award">Marvin Miller Man of the Year Awards</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig_Memorial_Award" title="Lou Gehrig Memorial Award">Lou Gehrig Memorial Award</a> for his community involvement.</p>
<p></p>

</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Thome was born in <a href="/wiki/Peoria,_Illinois" title="Peoria, Illinois">Peoria, Illinois</a>, on August 27, 1970, the youngest of five children. Everyone within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue-collar" title="Blue-collar">blue-collar</a> Thome family played sports: Jim's grandmother was hired at a local <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_Inc." title="Caterpillar Inc.">Caterpillar</a> plant solely to play for the company's <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> team; his father built bulldozers for Caterpillar and played slow-pitch softball;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humility_grace_country_power_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-humility_grace_country_power-2">[2]</a></sup> his aunt is a member of the Women's Softball Hall of Fame;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blue-collar_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-blue-collar-3">[3]</a></sup> and his two older brothers, Chuck III and Randy, played baseball at <a href="/wiki/Limestone_Community_High_School_District_310" title="Limestone Community High School District 310">Limestone High School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup> Thome learned to play baseball from his father on a <a href="/wiki/Tennis_court" title="Tennis court">tennis court</a>, and also played <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> in what he described as the "ghetto" of Peoria, noting that he was the only <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> kid there but that he earned the respect of his fellow players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blue-collar_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-blue-collar-3">[3]</a></sup> One day during his youth, Thome sneaked into the Cubs' clubhouse at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> in an unsuccessful attempt to obtain an autograph from his favorite player, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Kingman" title="Dave Kingman">Dave Kingman</a>. Though Thome received signatures from several other players, this experience influenced him to be generous with signing autographs for fans during his playing career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Like his older brothers, Thome attended Limestone High School where he achieved <a href="/wiki/All-America" title="All-America">all-state</a> honors in basketball and as a baseball <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup> Although he had hoped to draw the attention of <a href="/wiki/Scout_(sport)" title="Scout (sport)">scouts</a>, at just 175 pounds (79 kg) he was relatively underweight for his 6-foot-2-inch (188 cm) height, meaning that he attracted only passing interest—the average <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) player weighed 195 pounds (88 kg) in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blue-collar_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-blue-collar-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Thome graduated in 1988 and, after not being drafted, enrolled at <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Central_College" title="Illinois Central College">Illinois Central College</a> where he continued his baseball and basketball careers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup> After one season, he was drafted by MLB's <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> as an "afterthought" in the 13th round of the <a href="/wiki/1989_Major_League_Baseball_draft" title="1989 Major League Baseball draft">1989 MLB draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blue-collar_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-blue-collar-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Professional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_leagues_.281989.E2.80.931991.29">Minor leagues (1989–1991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Minor leagues (1989–1991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For the 1989 season, Thome was assigned to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GCL_Indians" title="GCL Indians">Gulf Coast League Indians</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">minor league</a> affiliate of the Cleveland Indians. He finished the year with a .237 <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, no <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a>, and 22 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Runs_batted_in" title="Runs batted in">runs batted in</a> (RBIs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> After his rookie season, he met "hitting guru" <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Manuel" title="Charlie Manuel">Charlie Manuel</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> who later became his manager and mentor. Unlike most Indians staff, Manuel saw potential in Thome and worked hard with him, particularly on his hip motion while swinging the bat. Thome later said, "[Manuel] saw something in me I didn't." During this work, Manuel suggested to Thome that he point his bat out to center field before the pitch to relax himself like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roy_Hobbs" title="Roy Hobbs">Roy Hobbs</a> did when batting in the baseball film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Natural_(film)" title="The Natural (film)">The Natural</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The work paid off; in 1990, Thome hit .340 and totaled 16 home runs and 50 RBIs playing at both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rookie_(Minor_League_Baseball)" title="Rookie (Minor League Baseball)">Rookie</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_A_(Minor_League_Baseball)" title="Class A (Minor League Baseball)">Class A</a> levels of the minor leagues. Thome spent most of the 1991 season splitting time between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double-A_(Minor_League_Baseball)" title="Double-A (Minor League Baseball)">Double-A</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Triple-A_(Minor_League_Baseball)" title="Triple-A (Minor League Baseball)">Triple-A</a> where, in combination, he hit .319 with 7 home runs and 73 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cleveland_Indians_.281991.E2.80.932002.29">Cleveland Indians (1991–2002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cleveland Indians (1991–2002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1991.E2.80.931997">1991–1997</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1991–1997">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:160px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ClevelandMunicipalStadium1993Interior_(Jim_Thome_crop).jpg"><img alt="Jim Thome batting left-handed in a game in 1993; he is amidst his stride forward, and is about to swing." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="158" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/ClevelandMunicipalStadium1993Interior_%28Jim_Thome_crop%29.jpg" width="158"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ClevelandMunicipalStadium1993Interior_(Jim_Thome_crop).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thome batting for the Indians in 1993</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thome made his MLB debut on September 4, 1991, as a <a href="/wiki/Third_baseman" title="Third baseman">third baseman</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1991_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1991 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a>. In the game, he recorded two <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hits</a> in four at bats (2-for-4).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-BR-13">[13]</a></sup> He hit his first career home run on October 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brhr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-brhr-14">[14]</a></sup> Injuries shortened his 1992 campaign, during which he played for both the Indians and their Triple-A affiliate, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs_Sky_Sox" title="Colorado Springs Sky Sox">Colorado Springs Sky Sox</a>. Across the minor and major leagues that year, he combined to hit .236 with 4 home runs and 26 RBIs in 52 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1993, playing mostly for the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Knights" title="Charlotte Knights">Charlotte Knights</a>, the Indians' new Triple-A affiliate, he led the <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a> with a .332 batting average and 102 RBIs, complemented by 25 home runs. This performance earned him a late season promotion to the major league, where he hit .266 with 7 home runs and 22 RBIs in 47 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>After seven consecutive seasons with a <a href="/wiki/Winning_percentage" title="Winning percentage">losing record</a>, "a new ballpark and a few offseason acquisitions coupled with rising young stars have made the Indians legitimate contenders" for the division title during <a href="/wiki/1994_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1994 Cleveland Indians season">their 1994 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kazzie_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-kazzie-16">[16]</a></sup> The Indians' core of offensive players included <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Baerga" title="Carlos Baerga">Carlos Baerga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sandy_Alomar,_Jr." title="Sandy Alomar, Jr.">Sandy Alomar, Jr.</a>, Thome, and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kazzie_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-kazzie-16">[16]</a></sup> A "promising youngster",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kazzie_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-kazzie-16">[16]</a></sup> for the first time in his career, Thome spent the entire 1994 season with Cleveland, playing in 98 games while hitting .268 with 20 home runs and 52 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-BR-13">[13]</a></sup> With help from the aforementioned core, the Indians held the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> spot in the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) and were one <a href="/wiki/Games_behind" title="Games behind">game behind</a> the <a href="/wiki/1994_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1994 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> in the standings for the <a href="/wiki/American_League_Central" title="American League Central">AL Central Division</a> lead before the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994–95 Major League Baseball strike">1994 players' strike</a> forced cancellation of the season's remaining games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Baseball_Chronicle_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Baseball_Chronicle-17">[17]</a></sup> During the strike-shortened season, Thome had his first career multi-home run game, hitting two solo home runs on June 22, 1994, against <a href="/wiki/1994_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1994 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a>' pitcher <a href="/wiki/John_Doherty_(pitcher)" title="John Doherty (pitcher)">John Doherty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brhr_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-brhr-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multi_hr_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-multi_hr-18">[18]</a></sup> It was not until <a href="/wiki/1995_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1995 Major League Baseball season">1995</a> that the Indians' success led to a playoff berth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> Thome was among the team's leaders at the plate, hitting .314 with 25 home runs and 73 RBIs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1995br_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-1995br-19">[19]</a></sup> and the Indians finished with a 100–44 record to win the AL Central but lost the <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Series" title="1995 World Series">1995 World Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1995_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1995 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> in six games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1995br_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-1995br-19">[19]</a></sup> Thome hit .211 in the World Series with one home run and two RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> Preceding the <a href="/wiki/1996_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1996 Cleveland Indians season">Indians' 1996 season</a>, sportswriters predicted that Thome would be moved up in the <a href="/wiki/Batting_order_(baseball)" title="Batting order (baseball)">batting order</a> and bat in the sixth position (he had hit anywhere from the fifth to the eighth positions during his first two seasons).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-multi_hr_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-multi_hr-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> During the 1996 season, Thome hit 38 home runs, once hitting a 511-foot (156 m) homer at Cleveland's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacobs_Field" title="Jacobs Field">Jacobs Field</a>, the longest home run ever at a Cleveland ballpark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-library_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-library-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before <a href="/wiki/1997_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1997 Cleveland Indians season">their 1997 season</a>, the Indians moved Thome, originally a third baseman, to first base after acquiring third baseman <a href="/wiki/Matt_Williams_(third_baseman)" title="Matt Williams (third baseman)">Matt Williams</a> from the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-library_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-library-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> That year, Thome helped the Indians set a new franchise single-season record for home runs (220), contributing 40 of them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Thome also totaled an AL-high 120 <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walks</a> to go along with 102 RBIs. Cleveland returned to the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">World Series</a>, but they lost to the <a href="/wiki/1997_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1997 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a> in seven games; Thome hit .286 with two home runs and four RBIs in the World Series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1998.E2.80.932002">1998–2002</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1998–2002">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The next three seasons were not as successful as the previous three for either Thome or the Indians. In July 1998, Thome hit his 24th home run of that season while helping the Indians end the <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a>' 10-game winning streak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> An article in <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> published in July 1998 commented that despite Thome's early career success (two All-Star Games and appearances in two of the previous three World Series), he was only "faintly famous" nationally and was not particularly well-known outside of Cleveland or his hometown, Peoria. His former teammate <a href="/wiki/Jeromy_Burnitz" title="Jeromy Burnitz">Jeromy Burnitz</a> said, "You can't really say he's underrated, because everybody considers him one of the top hitters in the American League, but he's surrounded by so many good players, it's hard to stand out on that team."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August, Thome broke a bone in his right hand and spent several weeks on the <a href="/wiki/Disabled_list" title="Disabled list">disabled list</a>, missing 35 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1999_pre_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-1999_pre-28">[28]</a></sup> He finished the year with 30 home runs and 85 RBIs while posting a .293 batting average. In Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/1998_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1998 American League Championship Series">AL Championship Series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1999_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1999 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a>, he hit two home runs off <a href="/wiki/Andy_Pettitte" title="Andy Pettitte">Andy Pettitte</a> en route to a 6–1 Cleveland victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Cleveland subsequently lost the series to the Yankees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postseason-results_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-postseason-results-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Headed into <a href="/wiki/1999_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1999 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland's 1999 season</a>, there were high hopes for the Indians; writers expected Thome to bat in the <a href="/wiki/Cleanup_hitter" title="Cleanup hitter">cleanup spot</a> of the batting order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1999_pre_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-1999_pre-28">[28]</a></sup> In May 1999, Thome hit a <a href="/wiki/Grand_slam_(baseball)" title="Grand slam (baseball)">grand slam</a> against Yankees pitcher <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Hern%C3%A1ndez" title="Orlando Hernández">Orlando Hernández</a>, which helped Cleveland to a 7–1 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In total, his batting average fell to .277, but he increased both his home run and RBI totals to 33 and 108, respectively. In Game 1 of the <a href="/wiki/1999_American_League_Division_Series" title="1999 American League Division Series">AL Division Series</a>, Thome hit a game-tying two-run home run off of <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lowe" title="Derek Lowe">Derek Lowe</a> that sprung Cleveland's defeat of the <a href="/wiki/1999_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1999 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> by a score of 3–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> However, after leading two-games-to-none, Cleveland lost the five-game series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postseason-results_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-postseason-results-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2000_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2000 Cleveland Indians season">2000 season</a>, Thome hit .269 with 37 home runs and 106 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> On June 21, he hit his 20th home run of the year against the <a href="/wiki/2000_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2000 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a>, marking the seventh consecutive season in which he hit 20 or more home runs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> On September 29, while in the midst of a tight race for the AL Wild Card spot, Thome led the Indians to an 8–4 victory against the <a href="/wiki/2000_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2000 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> by hitting a two-run home run. After the game, Thome was quoted as saying, "This team has battled all year, so this was nothing new. Here we are, and we're here tomorrow to play another day."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Despite finishing with a record of 90–72, the Indians missed the playoffs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cle_year_by_year_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-cle_year_by_year-35">[35]</a></sup> For the <a href="/wiki/2001_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2001 Cleveland Indians season">2001 Indians' season</a>, he finished second in the AL with 49 home runs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In addition, Thome had 124 RBIs and 111 walks. However, he led the league with 185 <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-7"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> He and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan González (baseball)">Juan González</a>, who totaled 140 RBIs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> powered the Indians to another division title. Despite these numbers, the Indians could once again only reach the <a href="/wiki/2001_American_League_Division_Series" title="2001 American League Division Series">AL Division Series</a>, where they lost in five games to the <a href="/wiki/2001_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2001 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thome had his best season <a href="/wiki/2002_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2002 Cleveland Indians season">with Cleveland in 2002</a>, leading the AL in walks (122), <a href="/wiki/Slugging_percentage" title="Slugging percentage">slugging percentage</a> (.677) and <a href="/wiki/On-base_plus_slugging" title="On-base plus slugging">on-base plus slugging</a> (OPS) (1.122), while batting .304 (16th in AL) with a .445 <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a> (second in AL). He also hit a career-high 52 home runs (2nd in AL) and collected 118 RBIs (seventh in AL).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The 52 home runs set a new Cleveland Indians' single-season record and made Thome the 21st major league player to join the <a href="/wiki/50_home_run_club" title="50 home run club">50 home run club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the conclusion of the 2002 season, Thome, who was a free agent, rejected the Indians' offer, to instead sign a six-year, $85 million contract<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> with the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> – he thought the Phillies were closer to winning a championship than the Indians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_article_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN_article-43">[43]</a></sup> With the Phillies, Thome's salary rose from $8 million per year to $11 million per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-BR-13">[13]</a></sup> Thome hit a franchise record 334 home runs in his first stint with the Indians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESPN_article_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN_article-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philadelphia_Phillies_.282003.E2.80.932005.29">Philadelphia Phillies (2003–2005)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Philadelphia Phillies (2003–2005)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg"><img alt="Thome with an outstretched glove about to catch a pickoff throw to first base; meanwhile, Terrmel Sledge dives back safely." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="634" data-file-width="800" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg/220px-Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg/330px-Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg/440px-Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baseball_-_sledge_making_base.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thome playing first base in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thome hit 47 home runs in <a href="/wiki/2003_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2003 Philadelphia Phillies season">his first season with the Phillies</a>, finishing one behind <a href="/wiki/Mike_Schmidt" title="Mike Schmidt">Mike Schmidt</a>'s single-season team record of 48 in 1980, and tied with <a href="/wiki/Alex_Rodriguez" title="Alex Rodriguez">Alex Rodriguez</a> for the MLB lead in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> On June 14, 2004 at <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Bank_Park" title="Citizens Bank Park">Citizens Bank Park</a>, Thome hit his 400th career home run, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Al_Kaline" title="Al Kaline">Al Kaline</a> for 37th on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_career_home_run_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball career home run leaders">all-time home run list</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> He ended the <a href="/wiki/2004_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2004 Philadelphia Phillies season">2004 Phillies season</a> with 42 home runs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWIB_15-8"><a href="#cite_note-WWIB-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2004, Thome won the <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig_Memorial_Award" title="Lou Gehrig Memorial Award">Lou Gehrig Memorial Award</a>, which is given to players who best exemplify <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Gehrig</a>'s character and integrity both on and off the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thome missed a significant portion of the first half of the <a href="/wiki/2005_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2005 Philadelphia Phillies season">Phillies' 2005 season</a> due to injury;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chen_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-chen-49">[49]</a></sup> he compiled only a .207 batting average with 7 home runs and 30 RBIs going into the All-Star break. He was only sporadically effective; one result was that Phillies fans booed him and cheered for replacement <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Howard" title="Ryan Howard">Ryan Howard</a> instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chen_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-chen-49">[49]</a></sup> He had season-ending surgery on his right elbow in August,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn20051125_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-espn20051125-50">[50]</a></sup> while Howard won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">NL Rookie of the Year Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The Phillies traded Thome and cash considerations to the Chicago White Sox on November 25, 2005, for outfielder <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Rowand" title="Aaron Rowand">Aaron Rowand</a> and minor league pitching prospects <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gio_Gonzalez" title="Gio Gonzalez">Gio Gonzalez</a> and Daniel Haigwood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn20051125_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-espn20051125-50">[50]</a></sup> Though the emergence of Howard made Thome more expendable to the squad, another factor in his trade to the White Sox was his family situation – Thome's mother, the "go-to lady" in his family and his biggest fan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> had died a year earlier, and he worried about his father. Since Philadelphia was willing to trade him, Thome waived the no-trade clause in his contract for the good of the team and requested that if possible, they trade him to Chicago so he could be with his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago_White_Sox_.282006.E2.80.932009.29">Chicago White Sox (2006–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Chicago White Sox (2006–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thome became Chicago's regular <a href="/wiki/Designated_hitter" title="Designated hitter">designated hitter</a> in April 2006 and flourished in his <a href="/wiki/2006_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2006 Chicago White Sox season">first season in Chicago</a>. He set the team record for most home runs in the month of April (10), overtaking <a href="/wiki/Frank_Thomas_(designated_hitter)" title="Frank Thomas (designated hitter)">Frank Thomas</a>'s previous record by one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> He also set a major league record by scoring in each of Chicago's first 17 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> For the season, Thome hit 42 home runs, drove in 109 runs, and hit .288, though he struck out in 30% of his plate appearances, the highest percentage in the AL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On May 1, 2006, Thome returned to Cleveland to play against the <a href="/wiki/2006_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2006 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> in his first game as a visitor at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jacobs_Field" title="Jacobs Field">Jacobs Field</a>, and received an unenthusiastic reception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 16, 2007, Thome joined the <a href="/wiki/500_home_run_club" title="500 home run club">500 home run club</a> by hitting a <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_Los_Angeles_Angels_season" title="2007 Los Angeles Angels season">Los Angeles Angels</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Dustin_Moseley" title="Dustin Moseley">Dustin Moseley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p22_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-p22-58">[58]</a></sup> Thome became the 23rd major leaguer to reach the milestone and the third in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007_MLB_season" title="2007 MLB season">2007 MLB season</a> (the others were Frank Thomas and Alex Rodriguez), as well as the first ever to do it with a walk-off home run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p22_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-p22-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Several family members including his father were on hand to witness the accomplishment,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> which occurred at a game during which the <a href="/wiki/2007_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2007 Chicago White Sox season">White Sox</a> distributed free Thome <a href="/wiki/Bobblehead" title="Bobblehead">bobbleheads</a> to fans. Thome celebrated by pointing upward in homage to his late mother as he rounded the bases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 4, 2008, Thome hit a 464-foot (141 m) home run—which at the time was the ninth-longest home run in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Cellular_Field" title="U.S. Cellular Field">U.S. Cellular Field</a> history—against <a href="/wiki/2008_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="2008 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Luke_Hochevar" title="Luke Hochevar">Luke Hochevar</a> in a 6–4 White Sox victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> He hit a solo home run in the <a href="/wiki/2008_American_League_Central_tie-breaker_game" title="2008 American League Central tie-breaker game">AL Central Tiebreaker game</a>, which proved to be the difference as the White Sox defeated the <a href="/wiki/2008_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="2008 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a>, 1–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Thome's hitting remained strong during <a href="/wiki/2009_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2009 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago's 2009 season</a> – he hit his 550th career home run.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On July 17, 2009, he hit a grand slam and a three-run home run for a single-game career-high seven RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> By the conclusion of the season, he had passed <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> for 11th place on the all-time home run list with 564 home runs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Los_Angeles_Dodgers_.282009.29">Los Angeles Dodgers (2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Los Angeles Dodgers (2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 31, 2009, the White Sox traded Thome to the <a href="/wiki/2009_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2009 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> along with financial considerations for minor league infielder <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Justin_Fuller_(baseball)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Justin Fuller (baseball) (page does not exist)">Justin Fuller</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Thome waived his no-trade clause because he thought the Dodgers could win the World Series, something he had never done during his career,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> but Thome's only appearances with the Dodgers were as a <a href="/wiki/Pinch_hitter" title="Pinch hitter">pinch hitter</a>, due to chronic foot injuries that limited his mobility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mlb-pinchhit_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-mlb-pinchhit-69">[69]</a></sup> An additional reason for Thome to come to Los Angeles was the opportunity to reunite with former Cleveland teammates Manny Ramirez and <a href="/wiki/Casey_Blake" title="Casey Blake">Casey Blake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> He hit .235 with no home runs and three RBIs while with the Dodgers (4-for-17). After the season, Thome filed for free agency, eventually signing with the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minnesota_Twins_.282010.E2.80.932011.29">Minnesota Twins (2010–2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Minnesota Twins (2010–2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Thome.jpg"><img alt="The moment of contact between Thome's bat and a pitch from Fausto Carmona; the image is distorted through the black screen protecting those sitting behind home plate." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2719" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Thome.jpg/170px-Thome.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Thome.jpg/255px-Thome.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Thome.jpg/340px-Thome.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Thome.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thome hitting a solo home run off of Cleveland's Fausto Carmona at Target Field, September 21, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thome hit his first home run with the <a href="/wiki/2010_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="2010 Minnesota Twins season">Twins</a> on April 8, during the Twins' season-opening road trip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brhr_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-brhr-14">[14]</a></sup> The Twins opened <a href="/wiki/Target_Field" title="Target Field">Target Field</a>, their new home stadium, on April 12, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Target_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Target-72">[72]</a></sup> This was the third time in Thome's career that his team had opened a new stadium – the <a href="/wiki/1994_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1994 Cleveland Indians season">1994 Cleveland Indians</a> when they opened Jacobs Field,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2004_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2004 Philadelphia Phillies season">2004 Philadelphia Phillies</a> when they opened Citizens Bank Park.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> On July 3, Thome hit two home runs, passing fellow Twin <a href="/wiki/Harmon_Killebrew" title="Harmon Killebrew">Harmon Killebrew</a> for tenth on the all-time home run list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The game was stopped and the Twins played a pre-recorded message from Killebrew congratulating Thome on the accomplishment, during which Killebrew noted he was happy Thome did it while a member of the Twins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Thome hit the first walk-off hit in Target Field on August 17, a 445-foot two-run home run in the bottom of the 10th inning against the <a href="/wiki/2010_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2010 Chicago White Sox season">White Sox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stretch_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-stretch-79">[79]</a></sup> It was the 12th walk-off home run of his career, tying him for the most all time (a record he subsequently broke).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On September 4, Thome again hit two home runs in a single game to tie and then pass <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGwire" title="Mark McGwire">Mark McGwire</a> for the ninth spot on the career home run list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ninth_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-ninth-81">[81]</a></sup> Thome surpassed <a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a>'s home run total on September 11, when he hit his 587th career home run in the top of the 12th inning in Cleveland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Toward the end of the season, Thome commented that playing with the Twins made him feel rejuvenated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> He finished the 2010 season with a .283 average, 25 home runs and 59 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Thome posted his best slugging percentage since 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2011, Thome accepted a one-year, $3 million contract with incentives to continue playing for the Twins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deal_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-deal-86">[86]</a></sup> On July 17, Thome hit the longest home run ever at Target Field, a 490-foot (150 m) home run into the upper deck in right-center field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> He hit his 599th and 600th career home runs (in two straight at bats) at <a href="/wiki/Comerica_Park" title="Comerica Park">Comerica Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a> on August 15, making him only the eighth player to achieve that home run total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_stint_with_Cleveland_.282011.29">Second stint with Cleveland (2011)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Second stint with Cleveland (2011)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 26, 2011, Thome waived his contractual no-trade clause to return to his first team, the <a href="/wiki/2011_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2011 Cleveland Indians season">Cleveland Indians</a>, in exchange for future considerations for the Twins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On September 18, the clubs announced that Minnesota had received $20,000 for him, which Aaron Gleeman of <a href="/wiki/NBC_Sports" title="NBC Sports">NBC Sports</a> called "silly" and "nothing"; Paul Hoynes of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Plain_Dealer" title="The Plain Dealer">The Plain Dealer</a></i> wrote that ticket and jersey sales alone from re-acquiring Thome covered the money they paid to acquire him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> On September 23, Cleveland held a ceremony to honor Thome, and revealed plans to erect a statue depicting him in Heritage Park. In the game, he hit a home run that landed near the proposed location for his statue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> While with Cleveland in 2011, Thome played in 22 games, predominantly hitting fifth in the batting order, and he posted a .296 batting average with 3 home runs and 10 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-BR-13">[13]</a></sup> Through 2011, he was second among all active major leaguers in career home runs (604; behind Alex Rodriguez) and RBIs (1,674; Rodriguez), and fifth in career slugging percentage (.556; behind <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, Rodriguez, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Braun" title="Ryan Braun">Ryan Braun</a>, and Howard).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Thome was the Indians' all-time leader in home runs (337), walks (1,008), and strikeouts (1,400).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_stint_with_Philadelphia_.282012.29">Second stint with Philadelphia (2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Second stint with Philadelphia (2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_on_June_9,_2012.jpg"><img alt="Thome has swung through a pitch during a day game wearing his gray Phillies uniform." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="660" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg/330px-Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg/440px-Jim_Thome_on_June_9%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_on_June_9,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thome during his second stint with the Phillies in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the 2011 season, Thome agreed to a one-year, $1.25 million deal that returned him to Philadelphia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> He called coming back to Philadelphia a "no-brainer" in his news conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> He also mentioned that, due to Ryan Howard's <a href="/wiki/Achilles_tendon" title="Achilles tendon">Achilles tendon</a> injury, he would "spend the offseason preparing himself to play first base once or twice a week", despite not having played defensively since 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Thome started his first game at first base since 2007 on April 8, 2012, during which he started a <a href="/wiki/Double_play#Common_double_plays" title="Double play">3–6–3 double play</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thome experienced stiffness in his lower back in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2012 Philadelphia Phillies season">Phillies</a>' game against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2012 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a> on April 28,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and early in May, he was placed on the 15-day disabled list with a <a href="/wiki/Strain_(injury)" title="Strain (injury)">strained</a> lower back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> At the time, he was batting only .100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Thome returned to the club in early June, and prepared for <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2012 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> as the DH. Thome finished the nine-game interleague road trip with four home runs and 14 RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 17, Thome became the fourth major league player to hit 100 home runs with three different teams, joining Reggie Jackson, <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Evans" title="Darrell Evans">Darrell Evans</a> and Rodriguez.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sweep_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-sweep-104">[104]</a></sup> Six days later, Thome hit a pinch-hit walk-off home run in the ninth inning off of <a href="/wiki/Jake_McGee" title="Jake McGee">Jake McGee</a> to beat the <a href="/wiki/2012_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2012 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a>, 7–6. This was Thome's 609th home run, tying <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a> for seventh all-time in home runs while also setting the new record for most walk-off home runs (13) in the modern era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Thome's last game as a Phillie was an afternoon loss to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Miami_Marlins_season" title="2012 Miami Marlins season">Miami Marlins</a> on June 30. After the game (which coincided with Howard's return from the disabled list), the team announced that Thome had been traded to Baltimore to serve as their designated hitter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_Orioles_.282012.29">Baltimore Orioles (2012)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Baltimore Orioles (2012)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_on_July_1,_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="620" height="355" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg/220px-Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg/330px-Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg/440px-Jim_Thome_on_July_1%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_on_July_1,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thome with the Orioles in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Orioles cited Thome's veteran experience on a playoff-bound team as a primary factor in acquiring him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Orioles <a href="/wiki/Catcher" title="Catcher">catcher</a> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Wieters" title="Matt Wieters">Matt Wieters</a> said of Thome,</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"I think you look at him and say: This is a guy who loves the game more than anyone. He's the first guy to the park, the first guy to the weight room, the first guy hitting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Profile_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On July 20, Thome hit his first home run with the Orioles, his 610th of all time moving him past Sosa for seventh place all-time, against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2012 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> at <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Field" title="Progressive Field">Progressive Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> On August 6, Thome was placed on the 15-day disabled list with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herniated_disk" title="Herniated disk">herniated disk</a>; he remained on the DL until September 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In his first game back, he drove in the game-winning RBI in extra innings against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2012 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> After beating the Indians in a game where he hit his 611th career home run, Thome said, "There's a lot [of] memories. I've had great memories on that side and then coming in here as an opponent against them. Any time you come home, they say, it's very special. It's even more special to get the W's. That's, I think, the main thing. The bottom line is I played here a long time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Orioles teammates remarked at Thome's commitment to talking about the game while in the dugout. Thome remarked, "I talk the game. When I set in the dugout during games I talk baseball to these guys. They'll ask, 'Hey, what's this pitcher like?' or 'What about the game?' 'What about all those Indians teams you were on?' I did it to <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a> when he was in his 40s."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Profile_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-109">[109]</a></sup> The Orioles made the playoffs, but lost in five games to the Yankees during the <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Division_Series" title="2012 American League Division Series">AL Division Series</a>. Thome hit .133 in the playoffs with no home runs or RBIs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-playing_career">Post-playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Post-playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On July 2, 2013, Thome joined the White Sox organization as special assistant to the general manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In the future, Thome aspires to be a manager, an aspiration that White Sox chairman <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reinsdorf" title="Jerry Reinsdorf">Jerry Reinsdorf</a> wholeheartedly supports; Reinsdorf commented, "He can be a batting coach. He'd be a great batting coach, but someday he'll be a manager."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> In March 2014, Thome clarified that he is not officially retired; while he "loves" his front office job with the White Sox, he would "have to take" a call about him playing again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> However, on August 2, 2014, he signed a one-day contract with the Cleveland Indians to retire officially as a member of the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_profile">Player profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Player profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offense">Offense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Offense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thome is regarded as a great example of a "pure" power hitter, as indicated by his .278 <a href="/wiki/Isolated_Power" title="Isolated Power">Isolated Power</a> (ISO) rating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Thome's consistency was a draw for clubs to continue to sign him, even toward the very end of his 22-year career and after most sluggers' productivity fades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBC_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-NBC-120">[120]</a></sup> In 2011, he was ranked the sixth-best designated hitter in MLB history by <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports" title="Fox Sports">Fox Sports</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-best_DH_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-best_DH-121">[121]</a></sup> During his career, he compiled a .284 batting average against <a href="/wiki/Fastball" title="Fastball">fastballs</a> but compiled just a .170 batting average against <a href="/wiki/Slider" title="Slider">sliders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_(cropped).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="564" data-file-width="419" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG/170px-Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG/255px-Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG/340px-Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jim_Thome_runs_to_first_base_(cropped).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
In the latter part of his career, Thome ran at a slower rate, partly due to injury</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since Thome was a <a href="/wiki/Pull_hitter" title="Pull hitter">pull hitter</a>, opposing teams often employed a <a href="/wiki/Baseball_positioning#Infield_shift" title="Baseball positioning">defensive shift</a> against him; by playing three infielders on the right side of the field and the outfielders towards his pull side, teams put themselves in better position to field batted balls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Lindy%27s_Sports" title="Lindy's Sports">Lindy's Sports</a></i> described him as an "extremely patient veteran slugger who launches cripple fastballs and breaking-ball mistakes to all fields", though they did note that he struck out frequently, had poor speed, and should serve only as a designated hitter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> During his career, he had strong power numbers; in 15 of his 22 seasons, he had a <a href="/wiki/Slugging_percentage" title="Slugging percentage">slugging percentage</a> of over .500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BR_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-BR-13">[13]</a></sup> He is an example of a "three-true-outcome" player; 47.6% of his career plate appearances resulted in either home runs, strikeouts, or walks, the highest of all time by nearly seven percentage points.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p4_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-p4-126">[126]</a></sup> He is a self-described slow runner, but has said that he always hustled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p4_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-p4-126">[126]</a></sup> He stole only 19 bases after 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defense">Defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thome began his career playing third base and did so until the 1997 season, when he converted to first base to make room at third after the Indians traded for <a href="/wiki/Matt_Williams_(third_baseman)" title="Matt Williams (third baseman)">Matt Williams</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Injuries, however, took their toll and confined him almost exclusively to being a designated hitter in the latter stages of his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBC_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-NBC-120">[120]</a></sup> Overall, he spent 10 separate stints on the disabled list, mostly for his back.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> By the end of Thome's career, his back prevented him from playing the field effectively<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> – he played first base four times with the Phillies in <a href="/wiki/2012_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2012 Philadelphia Phillies season">2012</a> which marked the first time he played the field since 2007 with the <a href="/wiki/2007_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2007 Chicago White Sox season">White Sox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> By the end of his career, writers described him as being a "huge liability in the field".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_characteristics">Playing characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Playing characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thome was known throughout the baseball world for wearing high socks and for his unique batting stance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup> In 1997, the Indians wore high socks for his birthday in August, but ended up wearing them for the remainder of the season out of superstition and eventually reached the World Series. Upon his return to the Indians in 2011, the club again sported the high socks as a tribute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> His batting stance featured him pointing his bat to center field prior to the pitch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Love_Letter_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-Love_Letter-138">[138]</a></sup> Thome adopted this stance from <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Manuel" title="Charlie Manuel">Charlie Manuel</a>, who was the Indians hitting coach, and since then Ryan Howard has also adopted it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Thome credits his calm demeanor to his role model during his early playing years, Eddie Murray, once commenting,</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"Eddie taught me to play the game exactly the same when you fail and when you succeed. Hit a home run, hey, enjoy the moment, but then let it go. If you strike out with the bases loaded, same thing, let it go. I don't smash helmets when I strike out, because it's not the helmet's fault, it's my fault."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thome's friendly personality has been the subject of much attention. In a 2007 poll of 464 MLB players, he tied with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Sweeney" title="Mike Sweeney">Mike Sweeney</a> for second-friendliest player, behind <a href="/wiki/Sean_Casey_(baseball)" title="Sean Casey (baseball)">Sean Casey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> After Thome hit his 600th home run, Twins closer <a href="/wiki/Joe_Nathan" title="Joe Nathan">Joe Nathan</a> said, "He is the world's nicest man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-road_to_600_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-road_to_600-141">[141]</a></sup> Teammate <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cuddyer" title="Michael Cuddyer">Michael Cuddyer</a> added, "He is the nicest, gentlest, kindest guy you will ever meet ... to everything except the baseball, he still hits that really hard."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-road_to_600_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-road_to_600-141">[141]</a></sup> His kindness comes up in conversations with many MLB players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Love_Letter_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-Love_Letter-138">[138]</a></sup> When he signed with the Phillies in the offseason before the 2012 season, Phillies <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_manager_(sports)" title="General manager (sports)">general manager</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Amaro,_Jr." title="Rubén Amaro, Jr.">Rubén Amaro, Jr.</a> cited Thome's constant positive attitude as a main reason for his signing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> As an exercise in remaining humble, he annually visited his high school prior to spring training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humility_grace_country_power_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-humility_grace_country_power-2">[2]</a></sup> A <i>Sports Illustrated</i> article said that Thome frequently signs autographs for fans and that he is "endlessly patient with requests".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_si_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-1998_si-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In a piece for <i><a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_(magazine)" title="Philadelphia (magazine)">Philadelphia</a></i> magazine discussing Thome's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> prospects, sportswriter Stephen Silver wrote,</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>"It's not just the numbers. Thanks to his gregarious personality, Thome is the rare athlete who played in several cities and was beloved everywhere he went. I saw the Twins and Phillies play each other in Philadelphia when Thome was with the Twins, and the same two teams in Minnesota two years later when Thome was a Phillie, and the opposing crowd cheered Thome both times, even when he hit home runs for the road team. Thome was similarly loved in his long stints in Cleveland and Chicago, as well as shorter runs in Los Angeles and Baltimore."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-philly-mag_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-philly-mag-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>A fan poll in <i>The Plain Dealer</i> in 2003 named him the most popular athlete in Cleveland sports history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_legacy">Career legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Career legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite his injuries throughout his later years, Thome totaled, according to <a href="/wiki/Fangraphs" title="Fangraphs">Fangraphs</a>, 71.6 <a href="/wiki/Wins_Above_Replacement" title="Wins Above Replacement">Wins Above Replacement</a> (WAR), a <a href="/wiki/Sabermetrics" title="Sabermetrics">sabermetrics</a> baseball statistic intended to quantify a player's total contributions to a team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> He was one of few players whose prime was during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_baseball_in_the_United_States#The_steroid_era" title="History of baseball in the United States">steroid era</a> and was not suspected of using steroids; Thome adamantly denies ever using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Performance-enhancing_drugs" title="Performance-enhancing drugs">performance-enhancing drugs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Soon after the announcement of his front office position (which signified the end of his playing career), writers began to speculate as to whether or not Thome would make it to the Baseball Hall of Fame, and more specifically, whether he would gain entrance in his first year of eligibility in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Writers also questioned whether Thome's candidacy would be hindered by his lack of self-promotion and others' tendency to overlook him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Thome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Thome and his wife, Andrea, have two children, Lila Grace and Landon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> He has also established funds to put his 10 nieces and nephews through college.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> During the offseason he lives in Burr Ridge, Illinois.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humility_grace_country_power_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-humility_grace_country_power-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/SportsCenter" title="SportsCenter">SportsCenter</a></i> reported that shortly after his nephew, Brandon, was paralyzed in an accident, he asked Thome to hit a home run for him; Thome obliged, hitting two in the subsequent game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Thome is also a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philanthropist" title="Philanthropist">philanthropist</a> and provided help to the communities surrounding the teams for which he played. In recognition of his community involvement, he was given the <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Miller_Man_of_the_Year_Award" title="Marvin Miller Man of the Year Award">Marvin Miller Man of the Year Award</a> in 2001 and 2004, and the Lou Gehrig Memorial Award in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> In 2013, after the <a href="/wiki/November_17,_2013_tornado_outbreak" title="November 17, 2013 tornado outbreak">November 17, 2013 tornado outbreak</a> struck <a href="/wiki/Washington,_Illinois" title="Washington, Illinois">Washington, Illinois</a>, just 15 miles from his hometown, he and his wife pledged to donate $100,000 to relief efforts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Among the philanthropic endeavors Thome and his wife heavily support are Children's Home + Aid, which strives to help underprivileged children predominantly with finding care (e.g., foster care, adoption, etc.),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hageman_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-hageman-158">[158]</a></sup> and an annual benefit to raise money for the Children's Hospital of Illinois, continuing a tradition his mother started years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Moreover, the Thomes try "to stay connected with at least one or two organizations in each of the cities" that Thome has played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hageman_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-hageman-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
